5
Discussion
5.1 Perspectives
Large scale industrial heat pumps are part of the future heat supply for the district heat network of Greater
Copenhagen. To what degree is not certain, as much of the heat supplied to the network will most probably
still be based on sustainable biomass. Still, as more of the heat supply is electrified, with a higher capacity of
electricity supplied by renewable and sustainable sources, such as solar and wind, the variability of the networks
will increase, requiring a higher degree of both heat and electrical storage, while also being able to control and
foresee the supply and demand of heat and electrical. Regardless of the systems chosen as part of the larger
electrical grids and heat supply networks, knowledge and experience with the systems is necessary for the smart
regulation and control of the grids. It is the hope of the author, that this project and the work put into this
model, will be able to generate new insight into the operation of large scale heat pumps, which should help
further the integration of this technology in the future energy supply.
Initially, of the aims of the projects, were to gain insight on the ramp rate of the heat pump and develop a
correlation for the coefficient of performance based on duration of time. The
Ramp rate and variability
One of the main targets of this project, has been to gain knowledge about the ramp rate of a large scale ammonia
heat pump for integration in a smart grid system. Conventional experience with large scale heat pumps in the
industry have been to stay well within the safety limits, when ramping the heat pump up for load, making sure
not to stress components unnecessarily. In the future heat supply, with large scale heat pumps supplementing
or possibly replacing biomass, it is important to know hos fast heat can be supplied and how much electricity is
going to be used from the grid.
The demand and supply of heat in the district heating network and power in the electrical grid is variable over
both short and long time-scales. Much of the variability is foreseeable, as much of it is dependent on domestic
and industrial behaviours and requirements, while some variability can be unexpected for various reasons. In
a future with a highly flexible power supply coming from solar and wind, with storage reserves for both power
and heat, energy fluctuations are a given. Knowledge of how fast (or slow) various technologies can supply and
consume is necessary.
As the electrical grid operates on a certain given frequency f = 50Hz not to damage equipment such as
generators and engines, constant regulation of the frequency of the net is necessary. The frequency is in direct
relation to the kinetic energy stored in the angular momentum of, for example a generator producing electricity
from the revolutions of a steam turbine in a power station. If the frequency goes out of sync, either by too much
or too little unexpected usage of power in the grid, it has to be regulated. This happens by starting up energy
producing or consuming systems, until the net is stable again. As a greater number of heat pumps on an even
larger scale than the one modelled in this project are expected to be part of the future grid, it is important to
118
==PAGE:134==
have exact knowledge of the performance and intervals which the heat pump will be able to consume electricity
and produce heat.
With a thermodynamic model, the ability to test various scenarios and control methods are gained. Detailed
information about the state and load in each components during load changes can be studied for prediction of
issues in components and to develop control strategies.
GAMS model
Different models for economic optimisation caused by implementing electrically driven heat pumps in the heat
supply network have been developed. One such have been developed at DTU, by PostDoc Torben Schmidt
Ommen [50]. The model is formulated in the GAMS modelling environment, where the parameters for the
modelareinitiatedbyMatlabandexcelsheetscontaininginformation. Itworksbyrunningaprizeminimization
optimisation, where the lowest economic cost of running systems dependent on a forecast of heat and power
demand. By using this model, the effect of implementing heat pumps along with other technologies have been
investigatedindifferenteconomicscenariosoftaxesandsubsidiesonfuelandelectricalsources. Theheatpumps
implemented in the optimisation scheme are assumed to operate with a constant COP, where the heat produced
bytheheatpumpsaredirectlyrelatedto, howmuchpowerisinput. Inthebeginningofthisproject, thepurpose
was originally to extend the relatively simple COP relation in the optimisation scheme, to investigate the effect
on the economics over a given duration of running time. For this purpose, it became necessary to model the
heat pump, as no exact information about start up operation of heat pumps were available. As the scope of heat
pump modelling expanded, and the model itself became more complex per necessity, time for implementation
in the GAMS model were simply not available, and this part of the project had to be abandoned.
Hopefully, the findings in this project might be used for gaining new insight and more detailed information
about implementation of large scale heat pumps for complete power and heat supply networks.
Balmorel
Another tool used for the heat supply and power grids on a wider scale and interconnecting trade of power
in the European countries is the modelling environment Balmorel. The software is open source, and has been
used in many case for analyzing power and heat supply network on national and international scale. It may be
used for analysing different given, current and future scenarios for optimising and looking into the effects of
implementing new technologies or varying taxes and subsidies on energy sources.
Policy, regulations and subsidies
As hinted above, there is no doubt that policies have a major effect on the integration of sustainable and clean
energy technology, such as wind and solar powered electricity, or the heat supplied by heat pumps, sustainable
biomass or waste burning. Many different technologies are available for converting one form of energy into
another more usable form, chemically, physically or mechanically. The consequences and effects, good and bad,
of using any of these technologies have to analysed in depth, for making realistic future scenarios and plans for,
how the supply should be structured.
One of the main methods for nurturing new and perhaps costly technologies, which ensure the safekeeping
and sustainability of the environment, are economic subsidies for the new technologies and taxing of fossil fuels
for ensuring that investments in green technology is economically feasible as well. As the technologies develop
and mature, and hopefully dropping in price due to better production method, secured supply chains and
development of technologies and material, the feasibility of the technology should improve, making subsidies
unnecessary. This has happened with solar power, where a major increase in production from China, has made
the panels considerably cheaper, while funding is still put into developing new and more efficient materials.
Convincing politicians that a new technology should be supported by taxation and support schemes is not
always a given. As such, the burden of investigation new concepts and laying the solid groundwork for develop-
119
==PAGE:135==
ing a better future, is often the responsibility of researchers attempting to gain new insights, even by sometimes
abstract ideas.
Developing more detailed and advanced models for future usage, is hopefully one step on the right path.
5.2 Model Improvements
During this project there have been a heavy emphasis on the modelling the details of the thermodynamic effects
over short time scales. This was done in an attempt to gain more knowledge about start-up time of the heat
pump and gain detailed knowledge on the ramp rate of the heat pump, as well as the effects taking place in the
heat pump components during changes in load over relatively short time scales.
Gaining knowledge of the ramp rate of the heat pump, and the performance during ramping, is important
for future cases and the implementation of large scale industrial heat pumps in the variable cost heat and elec-
trical grids.
Areas of improvement
• Advanced control methods & tuning
• Impulse mass flow model
• Condensation pressure control
• Detailed oil cooling components
• Extending component correlation validity
• Detailed geometrical modelling of SHT flow
• Ammonia condensation correlation
Control of the Heat Pump
As the complexity of the thermodynamic modelling itself was detailed and extensive on component basis, most
of the project was focused here. A relatively simple control method were chosen, with simple limiter conditions
for controlling when the controllers would activate.
The controller chosen was a PI-control, formulated as
MV(t) = MVstart + Kp ·

e(t) + 1
Ti
∫
e(t)dt

(5.1)
where the gains error gain Kp and the reset time of the integral part Ti were used for tuning the controller.
The control scheme is shown in Figure 5.1
120
==PAGE:136==
Figure 5.1: PI-control method
The only tuning of the controllers done, were to validate the controllers on a component basis, where the
controllerswereimplementedonasinglecomponentinanisolatedEESenvironmentfromtherestofthemodel.
Oncedesiredbehaviourofthecontrollerwasachievedandvalidated, itwasimplementedinthecompletesystem
model, were it was further adjusted slightly as other effects in the system could affect conditions.
Future perspectives should take into consideration proper tuning methods for the controllers, as this was not
a focus of this project. A short online survey shows several different tuning methods, each with advantages and
disadvantages. Below is only a few listed
• Manual tuning (trial & error) - Used in this project
• Zeigler-Nichols Method
• Cohen–Coon Method Method
• Chien-Hrones-Reswick Method
The different tuning methods will not be treated in further detail here, as this is outside the scope and the
area is a different study in itself. But an obvious target of further work on the model should be aimed here, as
the controllers have a major significance on the stability of the model.
Other methods of more advanced controllers could be considered as well, taking into consideration con-
troller behaviour during other scenarios besides the scenarios stated in this project, Steady State, Start-up, Load
reducing and Low load. A PID controller could be used, which is the same scheme as a PI-controller, but with
a differential part added.
Discretisation of volumes
A major part of the work on the model, went into modelling the major components in detail, to capture ther-
modynamic effects. This involved an extensive literature study on recent research, to use the newest developed
correlations for estimating the heat transfer coefficients in the relatively new design of plate heat exchangers.
This also involved modelling the heat exchangers with information about geometrical design and dimension-
ingforestimatingflowcharacteristicsandestablishsub-volumesfordiscretisationoftheheattransfer, tocapture
local heat transfer in precise detail.
121
==PAGE:137==
First attempt at estimating the heat transfer stepwise along the flow of fluid in the heat exchangers involved
establishing differential equations for each sub-volume, describing the state change of each sub-volume due to
fluid flow from adjoining volumes and heat transfer with the wall of the heat exchanger.
This approach introduced numerical errors when running a simulation, regardless of the scenario simulated.
A different approach was attempted, with linearising the state changes from inlet to outlet, only establishing
differentialequationsforthestateatheatexchangeroutlets. Thisimprovedupontheperformanceofthemodel,
with only small deviations in temperature at outlet, compared to the previous approach of each sub-volume
described by a differential equation.
Numerical errors

Figure 5.2: Performance of the parallel heat pumps, with numerical errors marked
When validating the components in isolated EES environments using the first approach, the heat exchangers
were validated for a wide range of starting conditions, different initial temperatures and varying mass flows,
proving to perform very well under a wide range of operating conditions. When the components were imple-
mented in the complete system model, numerical errors would be encountered.
The exact reason for the model encountering numerical errors is not clear. Looking into the residuals for the
solver, oftenshowedthattheequationthatcouldn’tbesolvedtosatisfactorylimits, wereoneofthesub-volumes
of the heat exchangers making a call for the correlation. This could occur in the evaporators, condensers, desu-
perheaters or subcoolers. It would seem, that during changing conditions as the heat pump would be starting
up, conditions could not be met. The water would be heating up, while the heat pump was running on mini-
mum compressor revolutions, and as the water feed pump started up, when conditions were met, to keep the
temperature offset by increasing the water flow, the compressor would be increasing speed, to increase the water
temperature. This would ensure that the compressors would be ’hunting’ the water temperature, as the feed
pump kept it low, ensuring the heat pump could keep up, while also not overheating the water. During these
changing conditions, the system of equations would meet a numerical error, where conditions for solving cold
not be met. The tolerance for residuals was 1 · 10−3.
Differences in temperature outlet
The differences in the approaches present small deviations in the outlet temperatures of the hot and cold fluids.

Other error sources
As no proper correlation for ammonia condensing in plate heat exchangers could be found in literature, a cor-
relation for R410 was attempted as a solution. The correlation used performed well enough for the model to
function. But attempting to find a proper correlation for ammonia condensing could potentially eliminate a
source of error in the model.
While modelling the geometrical details and dimensions of the heat exchangers, some generalised assump-
tions were made, about the characteristics of the flow. Especially for the shell & tube heat exchangers. The
refrigerant side is straightforward enough, with the refrigerant running in tubes. For the water side, the flow
123
==PAGE:139==
was just assumed to be cross flow, perpendicular to the tubes. In reality, the baffle plates and the tubes will create
considerable turbulence in the water flow, and likely increase the heat transfer coefficient on the water side. The
modelled desuperheaters and subcoolers might be performing considerably worse, than in reality. Modelling in
this area could potentially be improved upon.
Another approach that potentially could eliminate some problems with the model, could be to look into
the components being able to handle heat transfer outside of their limiting scopes, set by the correlations used.
The condenser correlation, as an example, is only able to handle conditions during two-phase flow, where the
vapour quality 0 < x < 1 is strongly correlated to the convection coefficient. During simulation, the condenser
outlet would often be in a state of subcooled liquid for a period, which was handled by assuming the outlet
condition was x = 0, when calling the correlation procedure. This was estimated to be a suitable solution, as
the dominant heat transfer is during phase change, and the period of subcooling at condenser outlet would last
for a short duration. By inserting a correlation for liquid cooling for ammonia in a plate heat exchanger, when
in this state, a more valid convection coefficient could be estimated.
For the desuperheaters the same was valid, as the outlet of the high pressure desuperheater was in a state of
condensing during some periods. This was handled in the same manner, by assuming outlet condition was a
temperature slightly higher Tout = Tcond + 1e −3, than the condensation temperature, ensuring the call for
the correlation procedure would work properly. This is due to pressure and temperature being constant during
phase change, which means no information about the state of the fluid is available, if no other information is
available, such as vapour quality or enthalpy.
Detailed modelling
Detailed mass flow
The approach of the model to model mass flow of refrigerant in the system, was to treat the mass flow from
component to component as variable, dependent on other components. Such as the compressor speed or a
valve opening. Meaning that if the high stage compressor increased speed, thus increasing the mass flow, the
mass flow across the desuperheater, condenser and subcooler would change instantaneously. In reality, mass
flow would be driven by impulse, where the kinetic energy of molecules in the flow would be exerted on the
slower flow in front of it, increasing pressure as well in the process, in essence setting of a chain reaction from the
compressor outlet to the outlet of the subcooler. A model of mass flow as impulse driven was not attempted.
A simplified approach to the problem, could perhaps alleviate problems in the model, as sudden incremental
changeofthemassflowfortheintegralequationsundoubtedlyhaveamajorinfluenceontheconditionalsolving
of the equations.
For the district water heating network, the mass flows were treated as variables as well, depending on the
overallmassflowfromthecapacityofthefeedpump,aswellastheflowsforeachheatexchangerbeingcontrolled
separately.
The heat pump model treats the flows as node points connecting each component to each other. In reality
there are of course pipes with refrigerant and water in them, connecting components which could be modelled
in more detail, improving upon the model, taking into account loss in dynamic pressure in fluids, as well.
Condensation pressure
The pressures at the lower and intermediary stage were modelled as depending on the vapour and liquid in
the vessels, the liquid separator and the intercooler. But the condensation pressure was modelled as depending
on a valve, which meant that the condensation pressure variable is able to change suddenly, depending on the
control signal. The sudden changes of condensation pressure in one integral step to another is a probable source
of error in the system during simulation. Improving upon the condensation pressure model, would improve
upon the model significantly.
124
==PAGE:140==
Detailed oil coolers
The oil coolers were simply modelled as bulks of volumes, containing a mass of water, without any special
regard to using correlations for convection coefficients in oil and water. As the heat that needed to be absorbed
from the oil was given by the compressor correlation, the outlet state from the oil cooler was formulated with a
differential equation, such that the flow of water to the oil coolers could be regulated to ensure the water outlet
temperature was matched and regulated as required. The oil flow itself and the injection temperature of oil into
the compressor inlet were treated as constants for simplicity. An area of improvement is possible in this regard.
125
==PAGE:141==
Conclusion
A numerical model for a heat pump in the current research project SVAF has been detailed and formulated
in EES. The model describes two parallel two stage ammonia heat pumps, with screw compressors, flooded
evaporators using ocean water as a heat source, an open intercooler, desuperheaters and subcoolers of the shell
& tube type, as well as plate heat exchangers for the evaporator and condenser. All these components have been
modelled in detail, to the extent possible for this project and with the necessary assumptions taken as needed.
Newest research in ammonia boiling in plate heat exchanger have been used, while no correlation for ammo-
nia condensation in plate heat exchangers was available.
The model has been used for verifying the operation of the SVAF heat pump, supplying heat to the district
heating network, with the compressors being driven by electrical power. Furthermore, the heat pump model
has been subjected to scenarios such as start-up and load reduction, to study the reaction and details of the
components being subjected to such changes.
For verification purposes, the heat pump was subjected to a conservative gain on the controllers for the ca-
pacity of the compressors and water feed pump. Experience from industry states that start-up times for heat
pumps normally happens in a duration of 5-10 minutes, which corresponded greatly with the model reaching
full load in just under 10 minutes.
The gain of the heat pump was increased, which resulted in a start-up reduction time down to 5 minutes.
Further reduction of start-up time might be possible.
Lowest load which the heat pump was able to supply, was in the vicinity of 2.8 MW, while still operating at
good efficiency with a COP of 3.3
With a detailed model of a large scale heat pump, which is able to operate over a wide range of loads, more
insight into the operation of large heat pumps should be generated. The model can be used for developing
more advanced controls algorithms, to avoid damaging the components during fast ramping. For the energy
supply of the future, which is likely to see a higher degree of integration of heat pumps of an even larger scale,
it is imperative to gain the needed insight into operating heat pumps intelligently, in the SMART grid of the
future.

mentioned data.

Design (PID 01) 
Chilled fluid: Sea water 
Chilled fluid inlet temperature: 4!C 
Chilled fluid outlet temperature: 0.5!C 
Heating fluid: Treated water 
Hot fluid inlet temperature: 50!C 
hot fluid outlet temperature: 80!C 
Heating Capacity 5 MW 
Alternative conditions (PID 02) 
Chilled fluid: Treated sewage water 
Chilled fluid inlet temperature: 10!C 
Chilled fluid outlet temperature: 4!C 
Heating fluid: Treated water 
Hot fluid inlet temperature: 50!C 
hot fluid outlet temperature: 80!C 
Heating Capacity 5 MW

A3 SOLUTIONS DESCRIPTION 
We have designed this unit based on your requested data. The units are in accordance with EN 378-2 and the 
requirements under the Pressure Equipment Directive 2014/68/EU. 
Skid unit 
The unit will be complete assembled in our PTC determined European manufacturing facility. The design is vendor 
standard with some deviations, separately mentioned in this quotation. 
Heat Pump Skid 
The unit will be completely assembled in our PTC determined European manufacturing facility. The design is 
vendor standard with some deviations, separateLY mentioned in this quotation. 
a. The heat pump is designed for installation in a plant room with a minimum temperature of 15!C 
b. Condensation can occur on the outside of suction pipe and separator vessel, in case of high plant room 
temperature and low suction temperature. 
c. Check design pressures are compatible with the refrigeration or water/glycol circuits connected to the heat 
pump 
d. The heat pump is designed to ensure a maximum 1 bar pressure drop on the secondary medium of hot and 
cold side. 
Refrigerant 
We have designed the unit considering R717 as the refrigerant. 
Compressor 
The selected compressors are Grasso screw compressors. Refrigerating capacity and shaft power according to 
EN12900. The capacities and shaft consumptions in the technical specifications below are nominal data. 
 
The de-superheater will be a shell and plate heat exchanger cooled by water and is vendor standard. 
Condensers 
The condensers will be plate heat exchangers cooled by water and are vendor standard. 
De-superheaters and Sub-coolers 
The sub-coolers and de-superheaters will be shell and tube heat exchangers cooled by water and are vendor 
standard. 
Liquid separator and Interstage vessel 
The liquid separator vessel is designed according to AD2000. 
Flooded evaporators 
The evaporators will be executed as plate heat exchangers. The vessel is designed according to AD2000. 
Instrumentation (pressure transmitters, temperature transmitters, etc.) 
Coils for solenoid valves for 230VAC voltage  
Regulating valves for 4…20 mA control signal and 24VDC power supply 
Flow Switches for 24VDC power supply  
Pressure transmitters with output signal 4...20 mA 
Temperature Transmitters PT100 Class A with three wires without signal converter 
Level transmitters for 24VDC power supply and 4...20 mA output signal 
pH meters for 24VDC power supply and 4...20 mA output signal 
All the analogue transmitter will be with output signal type 4...20mA. 
 
==PAGE:159==
 
- 8 / 36 - 
RT-IS-FI-2017-06.docx 
 
GEA Refrigeration Netherlands N.V. – International Sales 
 
Operating limits 
The heat pump design is based on a minimum water circuit pressure, constant water temperature and flow. Changing 
flow and temperature should be limited as stated below, and will result in different capacities.   
· 
Maximum rise and drop in inlet water temperature is 2K per minute.  
· 
Maximum entering water temperature must not be higher than the corresponding temperature of the 
pressure setting of the safety valve, including “safety chain” if applicable.  
· 
Flow may vary approx. 10% per minute. 
· 
Allowed flow is between 0,5 – 1,1 x design flow 
· 
Water circuit pressure needs to be above the saturated pressure of water, to avoid boiling. As an example, 
at discharge temperature of 130ºC the water circuit pressure must be 3barg. We will inform the minimum 
circuit pressure during execution.  
 
If these conditions are exceeded the heat pump will not be able to operate. Precautions, like buffer vessels and/or 
control valves, should be taken into account on the water side to ensure these conditions.  
Available Field of Operation for 5HP compressors 
 
Please note the safety chain is not taken into consideration in the field of operation. 
 
For systems with Water/Brine 
Warning: 
The water must have pH in between 7 to 10 and the chloride content <60 ppm, otherwise the plate material 
of condensers and others exchangers, must be for instance 254SMO. This is valid for open as well as closed 
systems. Of course attention must be paid to take sufficient preventions against calcium scaling. 
 
As well as above conditions, water at evaporators must be clean and free of solids and biological agents so 
no faunae or florae can grow inside. Any substance used to treat the water must be subject to GEA approval 
before equipment manufacture. GEA declines any cost or damage for material incompatibility with water 
conditions.

B7.3 
Piping 
The refrigerant pipes will be seamless carbon steel P235GH and designed according to EN14276-2.  
 
Our offer only allows for the ‘on-skid’ piping and does not allow for the interconnecting piping between 
the heat pump skid parts.  
 
The required fittings, brackets and pipe supports within the unit will be made of carbon steel, or stainless 
steel when in contact with stainless steel parts. 
 
The water piping is not included in our scope of supply.  
B7.4 
Insulation 
The insulation is not included as part of our scope of supply. Due to the size of the system, this should 
be performed onsite. We will provide the required thickness and specification of the insulation during 
detailed engineering 
 
On the low stages of the heat pumps insulation will prevent condensation on the cold services.  On the 
warm surfaces it will prevent the unnecessary loss of heat, which will lead to reduced efficiency.  The 
compressor discharge piping, desuperheater and oil separators temperature would be in excess of 
80°C. In addition to retaining heat in the system it must also be insulated to prevent injury. 
==PAGE:179==
 
- 28 / 36 - 
RT-IS-FI-2017-06.docx 
 
GEA Refrigeration Netherlands N.V. – International Sales 
 
B7.5 
Electrical installation 
Our electrical installation is limited to the control system, and the control wiring on each compressor 
package. No additional panels or power/control cabling is included.  
 
Every heat pump will be equipped with a standard OMNI panel delivered by GEA Grasso Berlin. 
The additional components can be incorporated in each GEA OMNI panel. The cabling of these 
components is not included in our scope of supply.    
 
OPTION PRICE Frequency inverters. type Danfoss FC302 IP54. 
 
Power Panel not included in our scope of supply 
 
The cabling is not included in our scope of supply 
B7.6 
Base frame 
Equipment will be packaged on a robust structural steel base frame. for direct placing on flat. load 
bearing concrete floor. Civil foundations must include provision for drainage to the water sewer. Access 
ladders. platforms and supply foundation bolts are excluded.  
B7.7 
Painting 
Painting where required. in non-insulated steel parts. will be suitable for machinery room environment. 
The frame will be painted. Other parts will be finished with primer only. 
 
Main components will be supplied with standard manufacturer coating/painting. The frame will be 
painted carbon steel. The non-insulated pipes will be painted. the insulated pipes will have a protective 
coating. Painting will be in RAL5014 and suitable for machinery room environment.  
Stainless steel components and aluminium cladding will not be painted. 
B7.8 
Inspection and tests 
The applicable welding of the refrigerant circuit will be verified accordingly the design code. A strength 
and leak test will be made. after closing the skid connection/nozzles. For transport. the unit will be filled 
with 0.2 barg of nitrogen. 
B7.9 
Engineering for all skids above 
The engineering includes the following things: 
- 
Detail engineering of the unit. 
- 
Selecting. ordering and inspection of the installation components. 
- 
Supervision of the workshop assembly activities. 
- 
Consultation with the purchaser. applicable approval agency if specified and sub-suppliers.

F ANNEX 
F1 
WATER CONDITIONS 
Values are valid for the following conditions: 
ü Clean surfaces without any deposits 
ü Sufficient water flow as per datasheet 
ü Absence of any other substances in inadmissible concentrations 
ü Absence of biofouling 
ü When using additives or cooling brines the suitability of the materials has to be checked in each case! 
ü please pay attention to cycles of concentration of cooling tower circuits. 
ü Values only valid for final concentrations - not for supply water! 
 
 
 
We reserve the right to adapt this data at any time without prior notice to include the latest researches.

D
Energy Roadmap to 2050
==PAGE:189==
2040 
Globally 100-300 EJ bio mass is 
used for energy purposes. Today 
the global energy consumption in 
the transportation sector is 100 EJ.
 IPCC - The International Panel 
on Climate Change
2050
The consumption of gas in 
Denmark is expected to be 75 
PJ/year, split equally between 
bio mass and electrolyzes.
Energikoncept 2030, Energinet, 2015
2050 
Denmark is independent 
from fossil fuels.
Folketinget
2035
3 GW solar power and 4 GW wind 
power has been installed in Denmark
IDA's energivision 2050, IDA, 2015
2035
10% of the Danish gas consumption 
is based on electrolyses 
and 40% on biomass. 
Energikoncept 2030, Energinet 2015
2030 
Heat stored in stones at high 
temperature (>600 C) is used 
for long term electricity storage 
at 50% energy efficiency.
 Allan Schrøder  Pedersen (DTU)
2030 
30 pct. of district heating 
comes from large heat 
pumps and water boilers.
 Anders Dyrelund, Rambøll
2030 
75 pct. of district heating is produced 
from sustainable energy – 10 pct. from 
solar collectors.
Energiforsyning 2030, Grøn Energi 2016
2025 
10 years of experience in 
operation of 40 MWh heat 
pumps in the district heating 
are collected from Stockholm.
Hammarbyverket, Fortum, 2016
2045 
Denmark is net importer of natural 
gas from 2035 and the North Sea 
is exhausted in 2045-2050.
Ressourcer og prognoser, 
Energistyrelsen, 2016 
2017  
Large flexible heat pumps (5 MWe) 
combine district cooling and heating.
Køleplan Danmark 2016
 Dansk Fjernvarme, 2015
2018  
A gradual implementation of 
taxes on biomass is necessary 
and has been acknowledged.
Brian Vad Mathiesen, AAU
2030 
One million cars should run on 
either electricity or hydrogen 
to reach the EU target.
Afgifter der forandrer, Klimarådet, 2016
In 2050 Denmark must be independent 
of fossil fuels. There is no simple and easy 
path to reach that goal. There is a variety of 
approaches that reach the 2050 targets. 
Development and implementation of new solutions 
takes time and that is why it is crucial that we 
start immediately. A large part of the knowledge 
and technology that will help us reach the 2050 
goal already exist. However, choices must be 
made. Partial solutions must be developed in 
time to help us in the green transition and the 
solutions that we choose must be implemented 
in large scale in time to make a contribution.

GEA Grasso M – Boosting 
efficiency
GEA Grasso M compressors are the first screw 
compressors with an integrated pressure-activated 
check valve ensuring low pressure drop. The integration 
of the suction filter and coupling housing greatly 
simplify assembly of the package. The outstanding 
energy-efficiency of these compressors is based on 
the infinitely adjustable capacity combined with the 
extended variable Vi-range. The variable speed from 
1000 to 4500 rpm (6000 rpm for C, D, E, G) ensures 
a wide operation range and maximum efficiency in 
full and part load. 
GEA Grasso M comes in eight model sizes and covers 
a swept volume range from 231 to 870 m3 / h at 2940 rpm 
(354 to 1332 m3 / h at 4500 rpm).
At a glance
•	 Outstanding energy-effciency
•	 Easy package assembly

GEA Grasso LT – Compact and 
powerful
The GEA Grasso LT series comes in sixteen sizes 
and with a swept volume ranging from 805 to 
11,467 m3 / h at 2940 rpm. Owing to the combined 
sleeve and anti-friction bearing to the rotors, 
the compressor has an extremely long life cycle 
and low noise and vibration levels. Connections 
are also possible for pressure, temperature and 
vibration sensors. The simple design features 
a smart integration of the oil management by

components allow easy assembly and service work

1 Generelt 
Følgende dokument har til formål at beskrive styringen af varmepumpeløsningen for projekt HOFOR SVAF II. 
1.1 Læsevejledning 
Det antages at dokument ”control concepts” læses før dette dokument. Yderligere uddybning og beskrivelse af HP 
autotune kan findes i dokumentet ” Overordnet Funktionsbeskrivelse HP Autotune og HP Doctor”. 
Referencedokumenter: 
 
PI diagram 
o 1160130 rev. V 
 
Komponentliste 
o Komponentliste rev. 02  
Referencer i dette dokument markeret med gul referer til tags som er udkendt på dette tidspunkt. 
1.2 Sætpunkter   
Generelt har alle setpunkter en neutralzone der er delt i 2 og lagt på hver side af setpunktet. 
 
 
 
 
 
 
Alle komponenter skal have mulighed for ’Automode’, ’Manuel start’, ’Manuel stop’ samt evt. ’analog manuel indstilling’ 
dvs. hastighed, åbningsgrad etc. 
Alle reguleringsmæssige parametre som setpunkt, neutralzone, evt. PID-bånd etc. skal kunne tilgås fra SCADA. 
Funktionsstatus på de enkelte komponenter vises i SCADA. 
 
1.3 Alarmer 
Alarm systemet skal være opbygget med 3 tilstande og visning af de 3 tilstande 
1. Ukvitterede fejl, er betingelse for en fejl tilstede og den ikke er kvitteret 
2. kvitterede fejl, er betingelser for en fejl er tilstede og den er kvitteret 
3. Kvitteret og udgået. Denne skal kun registers i alarm loggen 
 
Alarm grupper: 
Farve 
Gruppe 
Beskrivelse 
Rød 
A 
Alarmer som stopper anlægget 
Gul 
B 
Advarsler som indikerer problemer 
 
C 
Normale meddelelser 
 
 
Setpunkt 
Neutral zone

2 Overordnet regulering 
 
 
Skitse 1 de tre primære reguleringssløjfer 
2.1 Styring af fjernvarmetemperatur (normal mode) 
Reguleringssløjferne markeret med ① og bestemmer varmepumpernes kapacitet som function af vandtemperaturen. 
Hver varmepumpe har sin egen reguleringssløjfe, men deres funktion er ens. De lokale OMNI-styringer håndterer driften 
af kompressorerne men den overordnede PLC giver hver kompressor et kapacitets-referencesignal. 
Regulatoren måler fjernvarmetemperaturen på varmepumpens udløb. Hvis temperature falder sendes et større 
kapacitetssignal til kompressoren, hvis temperaturen stiger, reduceres signalet.  
Sætpunktet for ønsket FV temperatur indtastes i SCADA og anvendes direkte som sætpunkt for VP2. Sætpunktet for VP1 
er en procentdel af temperaturforskellen mellem indløbstemperaturen og sætpunktet. Denne procentdel kaldes for 
”fordelingsfaktor”. 
Example: 
SPVP2: 80 °C 
Tin: 40 °C 
DFHP: 65 % 
SPVP1 = (80 °C – 40 °C) · 65% + 40 °C = 66 °C 
Disse reguleringssløjfer befinder sig på PLC niveau. 
Label 
Eksempelværdi Type 
HP-op. 
FV temperatur 
80 °C 
Indtastning 
 
Fordelingsfaktor 
65 % 
Indtastning 
X 
FV temperatur ind 40 °C 
Visning 
 
Sætpunkt VP1 
66 °C 
Visning 
 
Tabel 1 Felter i SCADA 
 
==PAGE:209==
Version: 1.2 
 
Revision: 21-06-2017 19:58:00 
 
 
Page 6 of 18 
2.1.1 Lastfordeling 
Som udgangspunkt modtager både LP compressor og HP kompressor samme kapacitetssignal fra PLC’en. Det kan dog 
viser sig mere energieffektivt at forskylde denne balance så det ene kompressortrin tager større last end det andet. 
Der bør derfor indføres en lastfordelingsfaktor som bestemmer forholdet mellem de to kompressortrin. Denne faktor er 
en procentværdi mellem 0 og 100%. 
Hvis en værdi på 50% er indstillet, vil både LP og HP trin modtage samme signal. Hvis værdien er over 50% vil HP modtage 
en større værdi end LP trinnet. Hvis værdien er under 50% vil LP trinnet modtage en større værdi end HP trinnet. 
Værdien bør begrænset i et område omkring 50% da ekstremer som 0% og 100% ikke er formålstjenstlige da anlægget 
ikke vil kunne køre med denne indstilling. 
Herunder er et eksempel hvor kapacitetsreferencen fra temperaturregulatoren er 89% og dette skal fordeles til de to 
varmepumpetrin med en fordeling på 52%. 
Example: 
Refcontroller:  
89% 
LSstage:  
52% 
refHP =  
89% · (2 · 52 %) = 92,6 % 
refLP =  
89% · (2 ·(100%- 52 %) = 85,4 % 
 
2.1.2 Opstart 
Lastfordelingen er altid aktiv når maskinerne er frigivet for drift. 
2.1.3 Nedlukning 
Ingen særlige hensyn 
 
2.2 Styring af produktionskapacitet 
Reguleringssløjfe markeret med ② på Skitse 1. 
Det skal sikres at korrekt flow opretholdes på fjernvarmesiden. Samtidig skal det også være muligt at styre hvor stor en 
produktion i kW som varmepumpen skal yde.  
Dette kan gøres ved at sammenholde den ønskede produktion, men den ønskede produktionstemperatur og 
indløbstemperature. Herved kan det ønskede pumpeflow beregnes.  
Example: 
Qref:  
5000 kW 
SPVP2:  
80 °C 
Tinlet:  
45 °C 
refpump = 
5000 kW ·3,6 / (4,19 · (80 °C - 45 °C)) = 123 m3/hr 
 
En regulator styrer pumpens omdrejninger således at pumpen søger at ramme dette beregnede flow. Regulatoren måler 
det aktuelle flow med flowmåler xx og regulerer pumpen herefter. 
Label 
Eksempelværdi Type 
HP-op. 
FV temperatur ud 
80 °C 
Indtastning 
 
Ønsket produktion 4800 kW 
Indtastning 
 
==PAGE:210==
Version: 1.2 
 
Revision: 21-06-2017 19:58:00 
 
 
Page 7 of 18 
FV temperatur ind 
40 °C 
Visning 
 
Nødvendig flow 
123 m3/hr 
Visning 
 
 
2.2.1 Opstart 
Opstartssekvensen er forskellige fra den normal driftsekvens. Dette er nødvendig da der ellers vil blive cirkluleret mere 
vand end varmepumpen kan opvarme. Dette vil resultere i at for kold vand leveres til fjernvarmenettet. 
I opstarts sekvensen bør pumpen i stedet styre efter temperaturen som kommer ud af VP2 og søge at holde denne en 
smule koldere (justerbar værdi) end det setpunkt som varmepumperne kører efter. 
Regulatoren styrer pumpens hastighed således at vandet ud af varmepumperne holdes køligere på trods af at 
varmepumperne stadig sørger at opretholde den ønskede FV temperatur. Hvis vandtemperaturen bliver for varm øges 
pumpens hastighed. Hvis den bliver for kold sænkes den.  På denne måde vil vandflowet stige i takt med at 
varmepumperne kan afsætte deres effekt. Samtidig gøres det så hurtigt som varmepumperne tillader det da pumpen 
kontinuerligt vil ”jage” varmepumperne. 
Pumpen starter på et minimums omdrejningstal som indstilles i SCADA. 
Når pumpeflowet overskrider det beregnede sætpunkt for normal flow, skiftes fra opstartssekvens til normal drift. 
Label 
Eksempelværdi Type 
HP-op. 
Offset ved opstart 
-1 K 
Indtastning 
 
Startværdi for pumpe 
42% 
Indtastning 
 
Aktuel pumpehastighed 47% 
Visning 
 
 
2.2.2 Nedlukning 
Når varmepumpen skal stoppes, skiftes til same sekvens som ved nedlukning og de samme sætpunkter anvendes. På 
denne måde vil vandflowet falde i samme takt som varmepumperne lukker ned.  
Pumpen stoppes minimums omdrejningstallet nås. 
2.3 Styring af kilde-side 
Reguleringssløjfe markeret med ③ på Skitse 1 
For at opnå den højeste COP, bør varmepumperne køre med det højest mulige sugetryk. For at opnå dette bør kilden 
holdes så varm som mulig igennem fordamperne. 
En regulator skal derfor implementeres, som holder flowet oppe i fordamperne så temperaturen ikke bliver for lav. Dette 
gøres ved styre flowet efter en ønsket afkøling. Afkølingen måles mellem kildens indløb og dens retur. I SCADA-systemet 
indtastes en ønsket afkøling (fx 3,5 K). Regulatoren øger hastigheden på pumpen hvis afkølingen er for høj og sænker 
hastigheden hvis afkølingen er for lav. 
Label 
Eksempelværdi Type 
HP-op. 
Afkøling af kilde 
3,5 K 
Indtastning 
X 
Kilde temperatur ind 12 °C 
Visning 
 
Kilde temperatur ud 
8,5 °C 
Visning 
 
 
2.3.1 Skift fra seriel til parallel drift  
Anlægget er udstyret med en række motorventiler som muliggør omskiftning fra serie til parallel drift på kildesiden. 
Et sådan omskift kan kun ske når varmepumpen er stoppet og igangsættes via en knap på SCADA systemet. 
==PAGE:211==
Version: 1.2 
 
Revision: 21-06-2017 19:58:00 
 
 
Page 8 of 18 
2.3.2 Skift af kilde 
Anlægget er udstyret med en række ventiler som muliggør omskiftning fra havvand til spildevand og omvendt. Dette er 
ligeledes en operation som kun kan foretages når anlægget er stoppet og gøres via en knap på SCADA systemet. 
Når der skiftes fra havvand til spildevand, pumpes der spildevand ind og ud i havvandsudløbet, indtil ledningsevnemåleren 
detektere et niveau under XX. Herefter åbnes der for returløbet til spildevandet og udløbet til havet lukkes. 
Dette er det eneste tidspunkt hvor kilderne må blandes. Ventilernes endestop skal derfor respekteres i hvert trin inden 
sekvensen fortsætter. 
==PAGE:212==
Version: 1.2 
 
Revision: 21-06-2017 19:58:00 
 
 
Page 9 of 18 
3 Intern flow balancering 
Dette afsnit beskriver de reguleringssløjfer som ligger inden for varmepumpernes afgrænsning. 
3.1 Styring af sekundære flow på FV siden 
I modsætning til kildesiden, handler det på fjernvarmesiden om at holde den lavest mulige kondenseringstemperatur for 
at maximere COP.Dette kan opnås ved at lade FV vandet som løber igennem oliekølere og desuperheatere varmes så 
meget op som muligt, således dette varmere vand kan blandes med vand fra kondensatorerne ved lavere temperature 
og stadig opretholde sætpunktet. 
Det primære flow er det som løber igennem kondensatorerne, de sekundære flow er de delstrømme som opvarmes i 
oliekølere, desuperheater og underkølere. 
Styring af disse flow er nødvendigt, da for små flows vil give utilstrækkelig køling mens for stort flow vil sænke COP. 
 
Figure 1 Flow control at secondary heat exchangers 
En regulator for hver veksler (markeret med ①) skal således styre temperature som kommer ud af veksleren. Dette gøres 
ved at måle temperaturen med sensor xx. Denne temperatur sammenholdes med den ønskede temperatur (indstillet i 
SCADA) og ventilen regulere efterfølgende flowet. Ved for lav temperatur lukkes ventilen. Ved for høj åbnes den. 
En lokal pumpe sikrer korrekt forsyningstryk ved veksleren (samme pumpe kan betjene flere vekslere). Denne pumpe har 
en lokal regulator (markeret med ②) som virker på komponentniveau. Det ønskede sætpunkt sendes til pumpen fra 
SCADA.

3.2 Omkobling ved høj temperatur (højtemperatur-mode) 
Med høj fjernvarmetemperatur skal oliekølerne på højtrykmaskinerne holdes ekstra kolde. 
Hvis det ønskede sætpunkt for fjernvarme vandet er over en grænse på 88 grader (justerbar) åbnes ventil xxx og ventil 
xxx lukkes. Hvis sætpunktet stilles under grænsen igen returneres ventilerne til deres start position. 
Denne omskiftning kan ske i stilstand men også i drift. Der bør i SCADA systemet gøres opmærksom på at sætpunkter over 
denne grænse har denne konsekvens. Set punktet skal ikke kunne ændres så længe ventilerne er i bevægelse. 
 
==PAGE:213==
Version: 1.2 
 
Revision: 21-06-2017 19:58:00 
 
 
Page 10 of 18 
4 Håndtering af begrænsninger 
4.1 Kompressor units 
Hvis kompressorerne oplever for høje tryk, temperature eller motorstrømme begrænser disse sig selv via den lokale Omni-
styring. Håndtering af dette foregår altså på komponentniveau. Der er ikke brug for overstyring af dette fra PLC niveau. 
Det kan dog ske at en lokal styring producerer en advarsel, som reducerer i et stop. Hvis dette sker, skal alle resterende 
kompressorer stoppes også, da varmepumpen ikke kan drifte fornuftigt uden et kompressortrin. I disse tilfældes stoppes 
pumperne når de når minimum hastighed som normalt. Dette er også beskrevet i 8.2. 
4.2 Opfrysning 
Flowet gennem fordampervekslerne monitoreres løbende. Hvis flowet daler til under en given værdi og pumpen stadig 
leverer tryk, stoppes varmepumperne men vandpumpen fortsætter. En advarsel gives i SCADA. 
De lokale OMNI-styringer vil dog inden have begrænset sugetrykket og aflastet kompressorerne. Denne yderligere stop 
ved lav flow er en yderligere sikkerhed hvis OMNI’erne ikke når at redde situationen. 
Når flowet igen er på normal niveau, genstartes varmepumpen. 
4.3 Uhensigtsmæssig kildetemperatur 
I SCADA skal der kunne indtastes maximal og minimal tilladelig kildetemperatur for både spildevand og havvand. 
Når kildetemperaturen kommer indenfor 1 grad (justerbar) gives en advarsel i SCADA. Hvis grænsen overskrides i mere 
end 10 minutter (justerbar) stoppes varmepumperne normalt. 
Hvis kildetemperaturen ligger uden for de tilladelige grænser, kan varmepumpen ikke startes. Ved forsøg på start gives 
besked i SCADA om at varmepumpen er begrænset af kildetemperaturen. 
4.4 For ringe performance 
Hvis varmepumpen ikke kan opretholde sin produktionskapacitet eller temperatur og disse falder under en grænse i en 
given periode gives der først en advarsel i SCADA. Hvis problemet fortsætter i en periode mere, sættes en advarsel i SCADA 
og anlægget stoppes. 
 
 
==PAGE:214==
Version: 1.2 
 
Revision: 21-06-2017 19:58:00 
 
 
Page 11 of 18 
5 Automatfilter 
I normal drift overvåges filterets differenstryk via differenstryktransmitteren. Hvis signal modtages om at differenstrykket 
er fra højt, igangsættes back-flush sekvensen 
5.1 Rensning af filter 
Rensesekvensen har til formål at rense filtret således normal drift kan genoptages. 
1. Slam-ventil åbnes 
a. Åben position-feedback afventes 
2. Gearmotor og slam-pumpe startes 
3. Gearmotor kører i en fast tid (justerbar) 
a. Det afventes at tiden udløber (og filtret hermed er renset) 
4. Gearmotor stoppes, slam-pumpe stoppes og slamventil lukkes 
a. Slam-ventil monitoreres for lukket position-feedback 
Pumpen kører i en justerbar tid. Herefter stoppes pumpe og motor igen. 
==PAGE:215==
Version: 1.2 
 
Revision: 21-06-2017 19:58:00 
 
 
Page 12 of 18 
6 Personsikkerhed 
I maskinrummet er der 2 stk. NH3 detektorer (QA001 og QA002) og en nødventilator (M001). I rummet er også installeret 
et alarmtårn med lys og lyd (AL001 / AH001). 
Ved hver indgangsdør/port til maskinrummet skal der være en alarmboks (AT boks). Dette gælder også indgangen fra 
tavlerummet til maskinstuen.  
 
1.1 AT-bokse  
Der forefinde en boks ved hver indgang til maskinstuen. 
 
AT boksen indeholder: 
1 stk. nødstopstryk; dette tryk stopper hele varmepumpen på anlægsniveau. 
1 stk. alarmhorn; bruges ved NH3 alarm 
1 stk. alarmlampe; bruges ved NH3 alarm 
1 stk. drejeknap med hold; starter tvangsnødventilation 
 
1.2 NH3-sensorer 
Maskinstuen udstyres med 2 sensorer. En for lav alarm (500 ppm) og en for høj alarm (10.000 PPM). Hver sensor har to 
kontaktudgange som bryder samtidig. Sensoren for lav alarm fortrådes også via analog indgang for monitorering. 
Når NH3 koncentrationen overskrider lav-alarm, starter nødventilatoren (00M001), alarmhorn (AH010/AH020) og 
alarmblink (AL010/AL020) tændes. 
Når hovedalarmen (høj-alarm) overskrides, stoppes varmepumperne i maskinstuen, og alarmhorn/alarmblink tændes. 
Alarmhorn kan kvitteres ved tryk på SCADA, alarmlampen skal blinke så længe der er NH3-alarm. 
Der skal laves en mulighed for at lave et service-lockout på begge NH3-alarmer med en timer der udløber efter 60 min. 
 
1.3 Nødventilation 
Ventilatoren drives direkte fra frekvensomformeren. I tilfælde af nødventilation benyttes ”override mode” indgangen på 
drevet. 
Når knappen (PB002) til tvangsventilation drejes, starter ventilatoren via ”override mode”-indgangen og denne kører til 
knappen drejes tilbage. Der gives ingen alarm eller lyssignal ved denne manuelle operation. 
Det vises på SCADA at tvangsventilationen er aktiv. 
 
1.4 Nødstop 
Nødstop laves med nødstopsrelæ og overvågning af nødstopsrelæet. 
Der sættes alarm og indikation af i hvilket rum der er trykket nødstop. 
 
Tryk på nødstop på AT-bokse eller tavlefront stopper hele varmepumpen. 
 
Tryk på nødstop på kompressor stopper kun denne unit. Nødstoppene på kompressorerne er at se som maskinstop og 
ikke en del af et samlet linienødstop. Et tryk på maskinstop skal dog afslæses via netværket og PLC’en bør stoppe hele 
anlægget, da anlægget ikke kan køre tilfredsstillende uden alle 4 kompressorer. 
 
==PAGE:216==
Version: 1.2 
 
Revision: 21-06-2017 19:58:00 
 
 
Page 13 of 18 
7 Rumventilation og køling 
Udstyret i bygningen vil i drift producere spildvarme som vil opvarme bygningen. For at holde temperaturen i rummene 
på et passende niveau er der implementeret ventilation og køling i rummene. Dette afsnit beskriver styringen af dette. 
7.1 Kølevand for ventilation 
Vand fra indløbssiden af kilden bruges til at køle en pladeveklser med. En pumper cirkulerer vandet fra kilden og returnere 
det til samme streng. Således vil energien taget fra rumkølingen blive genanvendt i varmepumpen. 
En pumpe cirkerer vandet gennem vekslerens primærside og søger at holde en given temperature på sekundærsiden 
udløb. En regulator implementeres som øger pumpes hastighed hvis temperaturen bliver for høj, og sænker hastigheden 
hvis temperaturen bliver for lav. 
7.1.1 Opstart 
Pumpen frigives når vandtemperaturen er over et indstillet sætpunkt. 
7.1.2 Nedlukning 
Pumpen stoppes når vandtemperaturen når under et indstillet sætpunkt. 
7.2 Maskinstue 
7.2.1 Ventilation 
Indblæsningsmotoren drives af frekvensomformer. Indblæsnings kører altid, med mindre varmepumpen er stoppet. 
Ventilationen starter sammen med varmepumpen. Blæsermotorens omdrejninger reguleres efter tryktransmitter og et 
ønsket setpunkt i SCADA.  
Indsugningsblæseren er udstyret med et filter med tilhørende filtervagt. Hvis trykfaldet overskrider grænsen sættes en 
advarsel herom i SCADA. 
Udsugningsventilatoren kører efter et fast omdrejningstal. I tilfælde af ammoniaklækage overstyres motoren jf. afsnit ”1.3 
Nødventilation”. 
Ventilationen kører altid. 
7.2.2 Køling 
Hvis rumtemperaturen overskrider en grænseværdi (indstillet i SCADA) frigives blæserne på rumkøleren og den tilhørende 
cirkulationspumpe. Pumpen regulerer efter en konstant opvarmning mellem rumtemperaturen og returtemperaturen 
(eksempelvis 4K). Denne opvarmning skal kunne justeres i SCADA. 
Blæsere og pumpe stoppes igen når rumtemperaturen når under grænseværdien (minus et dødbånd). 
7.3 Tavle- og traforum 
7.3.1 Ventilation 
Anlæggets blæsermotor kører altid, med mindre det er stoppet fra SCADA. Blæser motoren regulerer selv lokalt efter 
korrekt trykfald over indblæsningskassetterne. 
Hastigheden på kølefladens pumpe styres efter rumtemperaturen. Ved stigende rumtemperatur øges pumpe-
hastigheden. Ved dalende temperatur reduceres pumpehastigheden. 
 
Hvis pumpen kører i længere tid (justerbar grænse) ved minimum hastighed, stoppes pumpen. Pumpen aktiveres igen når 
rumtemperaturen stiger. 
==PAGE:217==
Version: 1.2 
 
Revision: 21-06-2017 19:58:00 
 
 
Page 14 of 18 
7.3.2 Køling 
Hvis rumtemperaturen overskrider en grænseværdi (indstillet i SCADA) den tilhørende cirkulationspumpe. Pumpen 
regulerer efter en konstant opvarmning mellem rumtemperaturen og returtemperaturen (eksempelvis 4K). Denne 
opvarmning skal kunne justeres i SCADA. 
Pumpen stoppes igen når rumtemperaturen når under grænseværdien (minus et dødbånd). 
 
==PAGE:218==
Version: 1.2 
 
Revision: 21-06-2017 19:58:00 
 
 
Page 15 of 18 
8 Opstarts- og nedlukningssekvens af hele anlægget 
8.1 Opstart mode 
Følgende beskriver hvordan varmepumpen overordnet startes op fra stoppet tilstand. 
1. Hovedpumpe på fjernvarme- og kildeside frigives 
a. Herved vil disse pumper indstille sig på minimumsflow 
b. Flow igennem fordampere og kondensatorer vil være etableret som muliggør kompressorstart 
2. Sekundære pumper og flow reguleringer frigives 
a. Minimum flow gennem sekundære vekslere vil etableres og sikre oliekøling før kompressorstart 
3. Begge trin i begge varmepumper frigives samtidig 
 
De lokale reguleringssløjfer vil sikre opstarten og automatisk skifte til normal drift. 
8.2 Nedlukning mode 
 
1. Startsignal fjernes fra alle kompressorer 
2. Når kildepumpen og FV pumpen stoppes når de når deres repektive minimums flow 
3. Sekundære pumper stoppes samtidig med FV pumpen 
 
Maskinsikkerhed og ventilation kører altid.  
==PAGE:219==
Version: 1.2 
 
Revision: 21-06-2017 19:58:00 
 
 
Page 16 of 18 
9 Test-drift (Test mode) 
Grundet projektets karakter af forskning og udvikling, er anlægget udstyrret med en pladeveklser som muliggør en række 
tests, ved at kunne manipulere temperaturen på kilde- og varmesiden. Disse test modes er ikke en del af den normale 
drift, og skal igangsættes/stoppes manuelt fra SCADA. 
Specifik for disse tests kan varmepumpen køre i forskellige modes afhængig af det som skal testes. Disse modes er som 
følger: 
 
FRO 
 
FRA 
 
KTO 
9.1 Fjernvarmeretur opvarmes (FRO) 
I dette tilfælde reguleres temperaturen med temperaturføler (XX) på returvandet ind til varmepumpen ved at spæde 
fjernvarmefremløbet med ventil (XX) ind til returen igen. 
 
9.2 Fjernvarmeretur afkøles (FRA) 
Når der skal afkøles på fjernvarmereturen i stedet for opvarmning som beskrevet i 9.1 er spædeventil (XX) lukket og 
temperaturen på temperaturføler (XX) reguleret ved at øge flowet igennem varmeveksler (XX). Dette er gjort ved at øge 
omdrejningstallet for pumpe (XX) i henhold til setpunkt for fjernvarmereturen. Reguleringssløjfer FRO og FRA kører ikke 
på samme tid. 
      
 
Når dette mode køres skal manuel ventiler 1 lukkes og ventiler 2 åbnes på fjernvarmevandsiden. På kildesiden skal ventil 
3 og 4 åbnes og ventil 5 lukkes. 
 
9.3 Kildetemperaturen opvarmes (KTO) 
En mulig testmode er at bruge fjernvarme fremløbet til at opvarme kilden for at kunne afprøve værdier ved højere 
temperatur. For at gøre det er ventiler 1 manuelt åbnet og ventiler 2 lukket på fjernvarmesiden. På kildesiden er ventil 3 
lukket og ventiler 4 og 5 åbnet. 
I dette tilfælde er pumpe (XX) styret efter temperaturføler (XX) på indgangen til fordamperne. 
==PAGE:220==
Version: 1.2 
 
Revision: 21-06-2017 19:58:00 
 
 
Page 17 of 18 
10 Interface med HP autotune 
HP autotune/doctor er et computer program med formål løbende at kunne måle og korrigere varmepumpens indstillinger 
for at søge optimum COP. 
SCADA systemet skal kunne interface med dette system således at måleværdier stilles til rådighed for HP optimizer 
samtidig med at SCADA systemets sætpunkter kan korrigeres fra HP optimizer. 
HP optimizer varetager ingen direkte kontrol med anlægget. Programmet kommer kun med korrigerende sætpunkter på 
baggrund af målte værdier. Alle grænseværdier, indstillinger og sikkerheder styres stadig i SCADA/PLC/OMNI. 
I SCADA systemet skal som udgangspunkt bruge en række forudindstillede sætpunkter (en recept) som kan indstilles og 
anvendes til drift uden HP optimizer. Det skal således være muligt fra SCADA brugerflade at slå HP optimizer til. Hvis HP 
optimizer er slået til og korrigerer et sætpunkt er det vigtigt at det tydeligt fremgår at sætpunktet er overstyret fra HP 
optimizer. Dette kan gøres ved at sætte en orange ramme om de ændrede værdier. 
Hvis forbindelsen til HP optimizer forsvinder, skal SCADA systemet falde tilbage til den forprogrammerede recept. 
 
Funktionen af HP Autotune og Doktor er beskrevet i dokumentet ”Overordnet Funktionsbeskrivelse HP Autotune og HP 
Doctor”

∆P pump;1 = 1 [bar]

∆P pump;2 = 2 [bar]
(1270)
˙Vevap = ˙Vw;evapLP 1 + ˙Vw;evapLP 2

(1272)
